O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear sons, I have completed for you this book which is the last of the science of medicine together with its completion, and I have made the end through its expositions and through its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say, "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is neglected in our region and is completely and entirely suppressed, the science is lost and fragmented, and nothing remains of it except the brief descriptions in the books of the ancients which the hands have changed.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are obscured and the science is distanced.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	Now it seems to me that I want to revive it together with the ordering of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation;
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will add the forms of the cautery irons, and of the other instruments of the work with the addition of their declaration and preparation, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who undertakes it to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the arrangement of the limbs, and their forms and connections and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and muscles and their number, and the course of the moving and resting veins, and the place of their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And for this reason Hippocrates said that name without deed is much, and with deed is little;
et meismement en l’art de main.	and likewise in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you in the introduction to this book that he who is not knowledgeable of the things mentioned above, let him beware lest he fall into error and kill men;
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	as I have seen many times, many of those who meddle in this science and abandon themselves without knowledge and without experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish surgeon who cut an abscess of scrofula in the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries of the neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	because so much blood came out that the woman fell dead into his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another surgeon who extracted a stone from an old man, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	so he carried away with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I knew that if he was cut he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another surgeon who took into his care a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the fracture there was a wound;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the surgeon, full of ignorance, pulled the fracture over the wound with strong ligatures, and left no drainage for the wound, and left him in that state;
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and ordered him not to untie it;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and it remained so that the leg and foot were completely swollen and came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to come to him, and I hastened to come and untie the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I had untied it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But still, the corruption was already established in the limb, and I could not heal it;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and the corruption did not cease to spread through the limb until the limb was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another man who had an inflamed festering abscess, and then it became inflamed by the malice of his lord.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a canker, when it is pure of melancholic humor, it is not necessary to touch it with iron unless it is in such a place that one can remove everything that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And therefore, dear son, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, work where there is danger in several ways;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Therefore it is necessary that you guard yourselves, so that foolish people cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	So take up your instruments carefully, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best method so that through God's grace you come to salvation and are praised;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave the frightening diseases to serious treatment;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and remove your instruments from that which makes you doubt, and have faith in yourselves so that you may pass from this world to the next in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galen says in some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not undertake a serious illness unless you are called a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have divided this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapter is on fire cauteries and on cauteries of sharp medicine, and the chapter is ordered from the head to the feet;
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and of the forms of instruments, and of the cautery irons, and of all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is on cutting and piercing, and on cupping and wounds, and on the extraction of arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and the chapter is ordered and the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is on restoring dislocations and sprains, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and is ordered from the head down to the feet, and of the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we remember the work, it is necessary that I speak of the quality of the help and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of help and harm are the longest and subtlest science and the secrets concealed;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and of this many wise men spoke, and agreed on this;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and their words suffice me little, for I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery helps universally to every complexion where there is matter, except for two complexions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	that is to say, a hot complexion without matter, and a dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a complexion that is both hot and dry with matter, some have debated and said that cautery is a great help;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and others said the contrary:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cautery is not good for an illness that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and a hot illness should not be cured by heat, nor by dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and he who said the contrary said that cautery greatly helps a hot and dry illness that occurs in the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it sometimes by experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in any case, let no one meddle with it except he who has proven it, and who knows through long usage the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of the complexions of men, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the occurrences and the length of time;
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	of other complexions we have no fear, especially in cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians assembled and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cautery with fire is among the secrets of cures, and of greater benefit than cautery with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and comes only to the member which is cooked, and harms no other member except very little.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Burning medicines spread from one member to another, and bring to the member illnesses of difficult healing;
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and perhaps kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, because of its heat and the goodness of its substance, does not do this, unless there is superfluity.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found by experiment and by the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it was based on the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and for this reason I excuse myself for the length of the speech, for it does not please me that I should hide from you the secret which is contained in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives out the illnesses of the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating;
or le recevez en vos pensees.	or receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on the time when cauteries should be performed, and chose spring.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is suitable at all times, because the resulting harm is overcome by the help of the cautery;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and similarly if the cautery is for necessary, strong and urgent pains that cannot wait for a time when a greater illness might come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think of it, dear son, as foolish people do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for an illness that is cured by cautery does not return;
et il le dient ensi;	and they say so;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not as they think, because cautery is only a medicine that changes the complexion, and dries the humors that are the cause of the pain, and is better than medicine for the speed of its effect, and for the virtue of its work and its dominance.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is possible that the illness sometimes returns according to the patient's complexion and the location of the illness and its strength;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and superfluities are gathered in him by the consumption of foods and similar things, unless cautery is administered where there is little superfluity and moisture, such as cautery of the teeth for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return;
mais ce avient poc.	but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last resort of medicine, and it is true;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cautery is effective after medicine, but their understanding is false, and cautery is the last resort of medicine because when we administer various treatments for an illness and they are ineffective, then we administer cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clear that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the understanding of foolish people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that cautery with a gold instrument is better than with iron, and they did not say this falsely, but because of the quality of gold and the high value of its substance;
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the cautery site does not become putrid, but this is not true, for I have tested it and found that it is true in some men;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and cautery with gold is better than with iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And yet when you heat a gold instrument, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it is immediately cooled;
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if it is heated too much;
si font au feu;	they do so in the fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus there are enough impediments.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And therefore we use a fire cautery that we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have ordered this chapter from the head down to the feet, so that the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of the olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and coldness on the brain, and there are two that are made because of an illness that is called "soda," and because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and for a multitude of dreams and toothache and sore throat, and likewise for all illnesses that come from coldness such as paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by a purgative medicine purifying the head three or four nights, according to what the strength and age and habit of the patient can endure;
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then shave the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on his knees;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	afterwards place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and where your middle fingers will go, bleed him from there, then heat the cautery which is called "olivare", of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it on the spot marked with ink, and move it downwards and inwards with your hand little by little in a turning motion;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then lift your hand quickly, and examine the area to see if you see the bone a little;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	afterwards take a little salt, and put it in water and soak cotton in it, and apply it to the area, and leave it for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	afterwards apply cotton soaked in butter;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and leave it on until the burn is healed;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrapharmacon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the ancients said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it cleanses;
et por ce si aide mues.	and therefore it helps to move.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of them said that one should leave the cautery on so long that part of the bone is burned, and then one cuts away what is burned from the bone, and it is healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And others say that one should leave the cautery on so long, and press so hard that one burns away bone as wide as the whorl that women put in their spindles, so that the humors may more easily escape;
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one should leave the wound open for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	afterwards one should treat and heal it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cautery do not seem to me to be good at all, except in certain cases where there is danger;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems to me I should leave it there;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the head is weakened by the continuous secretions of nature, as we witness in other members;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and similarly when the patient's head is weak by nature, the first type of cautery is safer and better for me, and therefore I use this method for the overall good.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old head pain
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When chronic pain comes to the whole head, and lasts a long time, the patient should use herbs and pills which are called "cochie," and head purges, and oils, and plasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if cautery is performed as we have said before, and it is ineffective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care if the patient's head is of strong nature, and that it is not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	then cauterize a little below that cautery which we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	Then make a cautery on each horn of the head down to the bone, as we have said before, and make a cautery in the place which is called "vessels";
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and that is the place where cupping glasses are applied;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and lighten your hand so that you do not go all the way to the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak of it elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is necessary that the cauteries of the horns be more subtle than those with which one cauterizes the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	of the head cautery
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When a sudden pain comes to a part of the head, and the illness extends to the eye, and the head is purged by purifying medicines, and the other treatments that I have described in the division of illnesses have been done, and all this does not help:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	then I make cauterizations according to two methods, that is to say with sharp medicine and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cautery of sharp medicine is that you take a slice of garlic, and remove the rind and cut it a little at the two ends, and then split the temple where the pain is in such a way that you can place the slice of garlic under the skin;
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is placed, tie it and bind it well and leave it so for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then untie it and remove the slice of garlic, and leave the wound so for two or three days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then apply cotton soaked in butter until the suppuration comes out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	Afterwards, treat it with ointment until it is healed;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you wish, do this with some of the burning medicines that I have written in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery which is shaped like this:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a bell or it has a little curvature, and in the middle has a small opening;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and put it on the painful area, and hold your hand and turn the iron a little lightly, until half the thickness of the heart is burned;
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is outside, and an abundance of blood flows.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	Afterwards, put cotton in salt water, and put it on the area for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put cotton soaked in butter there, and then treat the area with ointment until it is healed;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery that is called "cultellare," use the point, and be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat a migraine as we have said before in the divisions of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cauteries previously mentioned, of medicine and of iron, are not sufficient, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery that is called "cultellare" until it is white;
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and bleed thus on the painful area a line half a finger long, and remove your hand once, and ensure that you do not cut the artery and that you do not go down to the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and beware of the mandible which moves when one eats, and let the nerve be such that it moves and that spasm does not come to the patient, and beware of the flow of blood from the artery when it is cut, or cutting causes great fear, especially to one who is not knowledgeable and experienced.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and leave the work half-done;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to stop blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you the place where it is appropriate in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that this cautery is not sufficient for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him in the middle of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed;
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you wish, administer the cautery that we have described in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two knives;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the earache from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes to the ear from cold, and solutions and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division have been used, and the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery which is called "points," of which this is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	Afterwards, prick all around the affected ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and move slightly upwards from the root of the ear after you have marked the place of the burn;
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and let there be ten points around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards, treat the place until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	Of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	A torture which ought to be cured by cautery is nothing but that which moves from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of illnesses;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not make any cautery for similar things which come from dryness and spasm of the nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you cure this similar kind of torture which moves from phlegm with bloodlettings and purgations of the head and with gargles, and this does not work, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with three cauteries:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the root of the ear, and another a little outside the temple, and the third at the joining of the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and place the cautery in the part which appears healthy, and make the cautery towards the head of the ear a little below the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as a thumb;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and leave the cautery on until half of the heart is burned;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is similar to the curette which we have shown before, but it is a little more subtle and the knife should be a little thicker;
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards treat the place as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and it does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then make four cauteries:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one in the place that is called "vessels" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and let it be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this illness, it is necessary to give the patient large herbs and pills that purify the brain;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	after shaving the patient's head completely, and applying to the occiput the mustard plaster which is described in the treatise on plasters;
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the manner of cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	if he makes it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he is healed thus, it is good;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if he is not, make three cauteries in the middle of the head descending to the neck, and let there be a space of one thumb's breadth between each cautery;
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and cure it like the others, and if you wish to add, and the patient can tolerate it, make one cautery in the middle;
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if necessary, two others on the two temples, and cure it until it is healed;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let the cautery be that which is called "olivare," as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of sores and what we have said before;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	after shaving the patient's head, then make a cautery in the middle of the head and on each temple, and one behind and three on the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the illness is severe, make four cauteries on the spine of the back;
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and leave them until the deepest part of the heart is burned, and lift your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	after the cure until it is healed, and let the cautery be what is called "olivare" that we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use fire cautery except those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to first cleanse the brain of humors and with other treatments that we have mentioned in the section when the patient is large and suffering to take medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot endure it, give him gargles and mastications cleansing the brain often with good foods;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	after shaving the head in the middle, and apply one cautery according to what we have said before, and one cautery above the vessel, and on each temple;
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the patient is strong and suffering, apply cauteries as I have said for one who has paralysis and bodily weakness, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to the method I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, apply one small cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When, due to melancholy, there are corrupt superfluities or humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize with such cauteries as we have described for one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if, due to melancholy, the superfluities are inclined towards melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then give him something to drink to purify the brain, according to what has been described earlier in the section.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	Afterwards, shave the patient's head;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	then make a well-made linen compress, like a circle, and place it on the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and the patient should sit cross-legged, and be well supported on all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	then present the liniment, and it is worth using old sheep butter;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and warm it over a fire moderately, so that the fingers, when one puts them in, can bear it;
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	then empty the circle inside onto the head, and let it cool;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this for the patient once each week, along with other good treatment, until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you wish to cauterize it, making several punctures throughout the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This method of cautery moistens the brain equally;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then apply cotton soaked in butter and chicken fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the water of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When water first comes to the eyes by the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something to drink that cleanses the head, and guards it from all moisture, and make him sweat in the bath several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	Afterwards, instruct him to raise his head, and cauterize him in the middle of the head, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of the water is to both eyes together, or one if the descent is to one;
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and with the whole cautery cut all the veins and arteries that are below the heart, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	and guard yourself against the flow of blood, and if you see too much blood issue forth, then staunch it with such power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision of the cautery how you will staunch it;
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and sometimes a cautery is made or a heating instrument under the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears from the eyes are old and accustomed and are upon the veins, or near the arteries that are in the appearance of the head outside;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and one sees that it is from cold phlegmatic superfluities, then make for him the cautery that I have spoken of at the beginning of the descending water to the eyes:
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I cautery in the middle of the head, and II cauteries on the II temples, and II cauteries on the nape of the neck under the two bones;
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if there is more need, then cauterize him wisely above the eyebrow with one small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the body of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you treat him according to what we have said in the division, and he does not improve, then give the patient to drink three boiled eggs;
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	after raising the head, and make a cautery in the middle of the olive-shaped cautery;
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and make two cauteries with the cautery that is called "clavilis" above the two eyebrows, a little below the hair;
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and beware of the artery that you do not cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the eyelid is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery which is called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you wish, make two cauteries above the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not leave the hand there except until the third part of the eyelid is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyes are turned inwards, and prick the eye, and cauterization is done in two ways:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	that is to say, by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they have grown and are even, then the patient puts [them] in your hand;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	afterwards draw on the paper with the eyes a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then put cotton moistened in egg white and parsley poultice on the eye, then heat the cautery of which here is the form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	Afterwards cauterize on the figure that you have marked little by little many times, so that the heart is burnt in that place;
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the sign of the success of the work is that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs raised at the puncture of the eye;
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	then lift your hand, and leave it so for three days, then put cotton moistened in butter until the burn is gone;
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if after that the hairs come, and the skin is softened then begin the cautery again on that same place, as you did before;
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hairs are missing, cauterize until the skin is raised to its natural place, and is even, and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The cautery of burning medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they are long and even, then make from parchment the shape of a myrtle leaf;
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	then take of French soap and quicklime, of each one-third, and grind them well together;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and do it quickly, so that it does not cool, then spread it on the form you have made like the myrtle leaf, and place it on the skin;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the disease affects only one eye, one should operate on one, and if on both, likewise;
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and place under the eye cotton moistened in egg white;
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and the patient's head should be on your lap, and place your index finger on the medicine, and press it lightly and move it every time the patient feels the medicine bite, for it bites like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine with your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the burning sensation has passed, lift the skin, and see if you see the membrane raised as if it were raised by the constraint of fire or by incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is so, it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not, put more medicine on the place where the medicine has not worked, until your work is even, and your eyes are focused;
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply cotton soaked in butter until the burning sensation has subsided, afterwards treat the area with the ointment called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary that you guard your work carefully so that no medicine falls into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the skin becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick at the eye, then restart the medicine on that area which is softened by the skin properly, as you did before;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	afterwards treat it until it is healed;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the shape of the myrtle leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size, and according to that should be your constraints;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and the right way should not be denied to him who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula, as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then you must cauterize it in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put his head in your lap;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and let the assistant hold his head between your hands in such a way that he does not move, nor shake his head;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	then put moistened cotton in egg white or parsley juice on the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	afterwards heat the cautery which is as follows:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and is shaped at the head like the form of a vulture's feather, together with which is the cautery;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you wish, let it be pointed from one end to the other, and if you wish, let it be like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but however, this one which is shaped is more valuable for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	Afterwards, press the fistula if it is open, and draw out the putrid matter, and dry it;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it is closed, open it, and draw out the pus;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	afterwards, apply the hot cautery, and hold your hand to the cautery at the part of the nose above the eye, so that your hand does not move foolishly;
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and put the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you reach the bone with the cautery at the beginning, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, repeat the cautery again, and another time if you need it, and leave it for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	afterwards put on cotton soaked in butter, and treat it with drying ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass without it being healed, apply a corrosive watery medicine until the bone is uncovered;
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and treat it according to what comes in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a type of cautery for fistulas that some of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Attend to the fistula, and cut the place;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	afterwards put into the incision a thin cauterizing iron of which this is the shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and it is made to the quantity of a third of a lead weight;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand with the cauterizing iron firmly, and let not the patient move at all, lest the molten lead run into his eye;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is necessary that one place on the patient's eye cotton moistened in egg white or in water:
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the lead thus burns the place of the fistula, and heals it by marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have described, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to make a hole in the nose, and to bring the fistula to the body of the nose according to what is appropriate in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	of cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Very often cracks occur in the lips which are called "chapped lips", and similarly in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks with what we have said in the sections, and the treatment is not effective, then heat a small, knife-shaped cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And apply it quickly to those cracks until it reaches the bottom;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards, treat the area with cerate until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	Of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess appears in the root of the throat, or in the uvula, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it forms pus and breaks and is old and becomes a fistula;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have said in the sections, and it does not improve:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then you must have a cautery according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after the opening or hole of the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches the bottom of it, and the last place;
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do so once or twice, after treating it as we have said in treatments, until it is healed;
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is healed thus, it is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	of the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines and that is not effective, then place the patient's head in your lap;
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	then heat the cautery, whose form will come later in such a way that you place a chain on the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and put the hot cautery inside quickly, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	then lift your hand and reapply the cautery according to your judgment;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	afterwards let the patient fill his mouth with salt water, and hold it for an hour and then spit it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way, the tooth that was loose is fixed, and the softened gums are restrained, and the corrupt moisture is dried.
de la dolor des dens	Of the toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When toothache comes from coldness, or there is coldness or greenness [a discoloration], and medical treatments are ineffective, then cautery is necessary in two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and cautery with butter and cautery with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Cautery with butter is such that you take butter of a cow, and put the end of it in an iron or bronze spoon;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	then take cotton and wrap it around the point of a tent [probe], and moisten it in the boiling butter, and apply it to the aching tooth quickly and hold it until it cools;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and thus do often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish, moisten wool and cotton in cold butter, and apply it to the aching tooth, and apply a hot iron until the fire reaches the tip of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The cautery with fire is such that you take an iron or bronze cane, and it should be thick so that the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	then heat the cautery, whose shape will come next, and apply it to the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled;
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter at the application of that cautery, and then rinse it strongly;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make a cautery of whichever head you wish, and according to what you have power;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the form of the chain:
des scrophules	of the scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the scrofula are of phlegm and cold moisture, and are not amenable to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery head, of which the form follows, and it has two openings for the fumes to escape from the cautery on the other side;
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or twice if necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it thus for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and apply cotton soaked in butter until the burn is healed;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards treat the area with ointments and tents until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cautery:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When humors overcome the channels of the lung, and especially when this comes from a cold constitution, then the patient must first be purged with laxative medicines;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	afterwards apply a cautery to the root of the throat, and be careful not to go down to the throat, and not to burn near the heart but a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	Afterwards apply another cautery to the juncture of the neck at the head of the spine, and let the cautery be that which is called "clavile" of which we have the form before;
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the place as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	immediately
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all the illnesses of the lung are from cold moisture, and the patient has neither fever nor dryness, and the illness is chronic, apply two cauteries on the clavicle in empty places;
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and one other cautery in the middle of the breast between the two nipples;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and let the cautery which is called "clavicle" be according to the form which is described above.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you wish, make a cautery by pricking with the entire cautery which is called "points", of which the form is described above, in the illness of the ears;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let the points be up to thirty, or thereabouts.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After, treat the place according to what is said before, and let the cautery have three rows according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for this reason the cauteries are lighter, because you make three at a time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Afterwards, let the patient be supported on his back and on his side;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	then lift the heart which is inside the pericardium with the fingers of your left hand;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated inside, then heat the cautery which has two nerves of which this is the form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the heart until it pierces to the side, and the figure of the cautery would come together with four cauteries;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and for that reason a cautery is made with the cautery which has three nerves, because of which the figures of cauterization are six cauteries;
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and the nerves are according to the thinness of a tent peg and this is the form of the cautery which has three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes one nerve is added to this, because of which there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	Afterwards, apply the cautery with crushed poppy seeds and salt;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	afterwards make the patient rest, and let the limb not be moved for a long time until it is well strengthened.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated upwards, which happens rarely, then make a cautery on the thickness of the clavicle, or many cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach there are chills and much moisture to the point that it alters its complexion, and catarrhs are multiplied in it, and in the accustomed methods of treatment, and it does not improve, then it is necessary that the patient be placed on his back, and extend his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	After this, make for him three cauteries: one under the hollow of the breast, of the size of a finger, with the entire cautery iron; and two cauteries outside the two sides so that the shape of the cauteries is triangular, and there is such space between one and the other that they are not joined together when they discharge pus;
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and let the cauteries be so deep that they reach the two parts of the heart, and let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without addition:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and he who is afraid of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and bleeding on the stomach at one point according to the amount you wish to draw out;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then cauterize with the whole cautery which is called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the cure that we have had before, until it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When pain in the liver comes from cold and moisture and great flatulence, so that it is far removed from its natural complexion by superfluities;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is treated with what we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit him, then the patient must be bled on his vein;
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and make three cauteries according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, outside the hypochondria, where the ribs of the man come;
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and let there be a space between each cautery the thickness of a finger;
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the cauteries be long in the direction of the body, and do not press your hand very hard on the whole cautery;
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and let only half the heart be burned, and let the patient be standing on his feet;
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot, let him be lying down, and extend his legs, and raise his arms;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if it is your wish, cauterize these cauteries with the cautery iron, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn the whole heart, for you would dry up the whole body;
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and that it does not reach boiling, for the heart is very delicate in that place, and know this for certain.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	if it is in the flesh, the patient does not feel very strong pain;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if it is in the membrane, he feels excruciating pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And then when this treatment weakens the eyes, it is necessary that the patient be supported on his head;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then bleed from the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to a ray, of which this is the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize with the cautery until the flesh is burned, and reach down to the fascia, until the perforation is completely through;
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment according to the treatment of wounds until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and it is not necessary that anyone use this cautery except he who has studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these diseases have been treated sometime.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can boldly operate, and yet it seems to me that it is better to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	Of the cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that for pleurisy one should make cauteries of the roots of aristolochia, and in this manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a root of long aristolochia, the largest that you can find, and let it be dry, and let it be as thick and as long as your fingers;
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and grind it in oil, and apply it to the fire, and cauterize; one cautery between the clavicle and the neck, and two small cauteries a little lower in the part that is below the beard;
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, leaning slightly backward;
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and one cautery in the middle of the breast, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two on the two sides of the breast outside the cautery that is between the two shoulders;
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	and do not press your hand, but act openly as if smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And some ancients said that some people use a fire cautery resembling a razor, and heat it and place it between the ribs, until it reaches that abscess;
