And when all the matter that is in the abscess is emptied, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat it with an ointment suitable for this until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofula, cut it as we have said in the incisions of scrofula, and if the wound discharges matter, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	Of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is broken, and the skin above is healed, many times an abscess results, and the same happens with an inflamed vein and abscess;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and one knows it thus when it is because of the artery, the abscess is long and deep;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel a throbbing;
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is because of the vein, it is round and apparent on the outside;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is folly to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits and in the groin and in the neck and in many other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is necessary then to avoid the treatment with iron, and that which is at the head must also be avoided, and in that which is an arterial swelling, it is cut above the skin lengthwise;
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then make the incision with the hooks, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues, until it is uncovered;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	then place a needle underneath, and make it pierce to the other side, and draw the artery out with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then prick the place which is between the two ligatures with a lancet until the blood which is there comes out, and the abscess is emptied;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then apply the treatment that generates pus, until the ligatures fall off;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with an ointment suitable for this, until it is healed;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	and if the abscess is due to the incision of a vein, then you must hold with your hand as much of the abscess as you can, along with the skin, then place the needle under the place that you hold with your hand, and make it pierce, and have a double thread there, so that you pull it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	then tie the abscess, as I have told you, with the ligature on one of the two sides at the two ends of the thread;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	and if you fear that the threads might come out, then push another needle with a thread under the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and pull the threads in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut the excess from the core and leave that which is tied;
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a cloth moistened in wine and oil, then administer treatments of tents and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses occur in the artery and the vein, abscesses occur in the nerves when they are injured, or by too much hard work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in the shoulders and the fingers and in all places where there are joints, and it is a serious abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in many conditions without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when it is squeezed strongly, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body, but under the skin;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and it moves well in all directions, and it does not go forward or backward, or down or up, and the one that is in the joints should not be cut with iron:
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	by chance, there would be a contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and the one that is on the head or on the forehead, cut the skin with a spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, hold it with tongs, and cut it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, lift it with a hook, and peel it, then remove it and close the wound with suture, and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of the large hanging lumps
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	Sometimes it happens in the abdomen and nowhere else, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" because of its resemblance, and its root is thin, and its head large;
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and there are small ones and very large ones;
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw a man who had two in his belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had thin roots, and were split, and moisture constantly flowed from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them and found one weighing eighteen ounces, and the other six and a half, and the procedure in the incision is that you observe if the patient is moist, and the color of the lump is white and moist and of thin root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	if so, cut it with a wide spatula, and have the fire cautery ready.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For in cutting, there often comes too great a flow of blood, and if the blood overcomes you, then hasten to cauterize;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision of the iron, take a well-made lead thread, and tie the lump with it as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then restrain it, and do not cease to tighten the lead thread until it cuts the lump, and it falls away through it without effort;
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are large, there is fear in cutting even for the belly, but you can well cut half, then cauterize it so that it does not return;
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cure the wound, and be careful not to cut the small swelling which is of a livid color and of poor sensation and of milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is a cancerous abscess, and I will come to the cure of cancer afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil bursts forth
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the boil comes from a cauterized wound or a fissure of the fascia, and is on the belly and some of the boils come forth, as happens in other ruptures, or from blood flowing from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from flatulence;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is by the rupture of the fascia and by the protrusion of the bowel, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens with diverse issue.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the protrusion of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it with one's fingers it goes back in, and then returns, and perhaps it is scarred, and increases greatly at the beginning of the bath and through hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, and does not constrain.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to blood, then the abscesses appear large and hard through these signs, and are fixed according to a quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to flatulence, it is soft to the touch, and the procedure is that you look if the appearance is due to arterial blood, or venous blood, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	Then you must leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, because of the artery and because of the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bowel, then you must instruct the patient to hold his breath, and lie completely straight, then bleed all around the swelling;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then instruct him to lie often between your hands, then go around the place you have marked with all the spatula, then extend half of the abscess upwards with all the large hook;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it around with a strong thread, or a cord of strong silk firmly, and let the knot of the tie be secure;
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then open the half of the abscess extended above the tie, and put your index finger there, and search for the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it caught by the tie, then untie it, and put the intestine outside the belly;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the bowel, then take it with the hook, and cut off the excess;
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein opposes you, then go carefully around it, then return to your work and take two needles, and thread two strong threads, and place the two needles around what you have done in a cross that you made pierce;
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then tie the abscess in four places above the needles, and if you wish, remove the needles, and leave the place until it festers, and the dead flesh falls off by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you cut it when it is thin and rotten, then treat it as is necessary, and heal the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place as is necessary, and sew up the place.
dou chancre	Of the cancer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have described in the division the types of cancer, and how one should work on it with medicines, and how one should avoid the iron treatment;
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and we say that cancer grows in the marrow, and there is great caution in its treatment, and the ancients said that when cancer is in a place where it can be excised, such as cancer that is in the breasts, and in the thigh, and in similar places, one should remove it entirely when it is in the beginning;
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is large and old, then you should not approach it, for I never could heal any;
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	nor did anyone ever heal any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the procedure, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile sometimes;
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then make him bleed if he has manifest repletion, then prepare the patient in a good place to perform the procedure;
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then apply your ointments to the cancer, and shave the hair from all sides, and remove it from all sides without leaving anything;
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow completely, and wipe the area well with your hand or something else, and if the flow of blood prevents you from incising the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the bleeding is stopped;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de ydropisie	Of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have, I said in the division, the types of dropsy, and in what manner the collection of water is made, and the signs of each type, and the treatment which is done by medicines, and that which is treated by iron:
si est eclites soulement;	if it is only burst;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one should not touch with iron in these two types:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	that is to say, tympanites and hyposarca, for it is a mortal thing;
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	then when you treat this type of dropsy which is called "eclites" with medicines, and the treatment is not effective, see if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as cough and diarrhea and similar things;
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	do not touch with iron there, for there is doubt;
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see the patient of strong constitution, and he has no other illness than dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should work thus:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	lift the patient straight up on your hands, and press his belly, pushing the water to the lowest part of the chest, then take the spatumile espinous according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be sharp on two sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	pointed, and yet not so penetrating that it can reach the intestine when inserted, and cannot injure it;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	then look if the dropsy is swollen towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	if so, you must make three incisions above the groin, straight down from above the hip;
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, let your incision be on the left of the groin, three fingers wide;
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it is due to the spleen, let it be on the right, and it is not necessary that the patient lie on the incision lest the superfluities run to that weak place;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	then pierce the entire skin with the instrument, and push it in, and lift your hand with the spatula between the skin and the syfac as in flaying, to the extent of a fingernail or thereabouts;
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	then pierce the syfac until the spatula reaches the empty space, and this is the place of the water, then pull it out, and insert this instrument, of which this is the shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it is similar to a thin silver tube, and is made of bronze or light iron, and has at the bottom end one small hole;
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and on one side, three holes;
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and two on the other side, and one on the other;
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and the head is cut like a pen, and this is the shape of the incision with which the scribes cut the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	at the top is the handle, so that when the instrument reaches the water, it immediately descends on the instrument;
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	empty then half or a third part, for if you empty more than is necessary at that time, perhaps the patient will die from the dissolution of his vital spirit, or he will faint, or he will approach death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but empty according to the quantity of his strength, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's strength signify, and his pulse;
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	then withdraw the instrument and retain the water, and it is retained immediately by the heart which stops the hole which is on the surface, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner;
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	then restart the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering that, and draw out a small quantity of water;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	do this for a few days, and be careful not to be foolish until there remains only a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you are doubtful about the patient, and you leave too much water, then treat him with a hot poultice or sand, and by much sweating or bathing and in the sun, and let him abstain from drinking;
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and treat him with drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stoppage of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who have no opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	Then it is necessary that it be pierced immediately with a very fine spatula according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	then place in the opening a thin lead tube, and tie it and keep it thus for three or four days; and when he wants to urinate, let the tube be removed, and let him urinate, and then put it back;
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and perhaps it is not necessary, for the urine that comes forth will not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose opening is small, is treated with the lead tube, as we have said, so it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the opening in its proper place are injured, for some are born who have the opening at the head of the penis, wherefore they cannot urinate unless they raise their penis upward;
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and cannot reproduce because the matter cannot reach the womb, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies often on his back, then they straighten the head of the penis and cut it like the quill of a pen, so that the opening falls in the middle, as it should;
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and beware of the flow of blood which often comes there, and if it happens, stop it with what stops blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Often these whitlows come on the penis, and it is an ugly appearance of flesh;
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and some are malignant and some are not;
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	then you should take them with a sharp lancet, and cut and cleanse them all, then apply moistened cotton with Egyptian ointment;
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the whitlow is malignant, of a foul color and fetid, then you must apply cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have incised it, and if the whitlow is on the finger, and part of it is inside the skin and part outside, then you must remove the whitlow that is inside first;
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	and when it is removed, then treat the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you treat it together, the finger is not safe from being pierced, and blackness and corruption come to the finger and the testicle;
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	it is necessary to remove all that is black and corrupt, then apply a plaster of honey and flour made from the bark of pomegranates and vetches, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a flow of blood occurs, apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The cautery helps with both dispositions together:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	that is to say, to the flow of blood, and to the corruption;
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the head of the penis is corrupt and retracted, it is necessary that you insert into the urethra a lead tube, and the patient urinates through it;
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	and when the skin is drawn over the head of the penis, which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or which happens due to a wound or abscess, then it is necessary that you scrape it with a sharp instrument, until the binding is loosened, and the head of the penis is freed on all sides;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	and if it is too difficult to remove this, it is necessary that you scrape it with a spatula, a little bit of the head of the penis and of the skin;
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	then separate gently the two, and place there a thin linen cloth moistened in cold water, so that it does not close again.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not a separation of continuity like other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	however, when we perform this operation of our own will, and properly on children, it is necessary that we perform the best work, and the easiest for healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not describe the circumcision of their children, for they do not use it in their law, and we have nothing but what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have seen the majority of the masters and surgeons who performed circumcision around I dal, and forcefully, and with a whole scalpel;
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	the heart would flee because there are two membranes, and by chance one cuts the upper one and the lower one remains.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	Now it is necessary to cut it, and the pain is doubled, and the purification which is of the dal is not assured by the point of the member;
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and in the purification of the nail, the iron sometimes slips, and the work is spoiled, and often they are born thus that they have no need of purification, and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the purification which is done forcefully with a linen thread, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, you cut equally in one single time;
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but that the thread be well tight around the skin;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and the manner of the first operation is that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only tying the thread around the penis, and then make him rejoice in all the ways that you can;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	then make him stand straight between your hands, and place the threads between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments;
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	then put your hand to the penis and blow on the heart, and pull it upwards until the head of the penis is inside;
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	then cleanse it well of the dirt that has gathered there, then mark the place with a double thread, then tie it below, one little tie to another;
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and hold it with two fingers for the second hour by the little finger and the index finger, and cut between the two ties, then quickly lift the heart and pull the head of the penis;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let the blood flow little by little, for that is the best;
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder on, and on the powder a cloth glued with a mixture of cooked egg yolk thinned with rosewater, mixed with good fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of the forces for the cleansing is this:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	the two ends should be sharp and cutting, and the ends should be as large as the handle, equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	The error of cleansing is when the pus flees at the incision;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	then you must spread it with your fingernail, before the place forms an abscess;
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then hold it with tongs, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if three days pass, and what is under the penis is swollen, leave it until the swelling of the abscess is calmed, and lightly scrape it;
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	cut it as much as you can move, and guard the part of the penis, this will not harm it at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Then treat the place of things inside a wound with powder, which we have said in the treatise on powders, and if one cuts too deeply into the heart and it goes to the top, it will not harm;
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Of the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is from obstruction by stone, or congealed blood, or bowel, or dead flesh, or similar things, which we have said in the division;
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone which is in or near the neck of the bladder, then the patient should be bent over on his knees;
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	and his feet should be placed on his back, and he should extend his belly from the upper part of his back, and the patient should restrain his breath as much as he can;
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and then the neck of the bladder is constrained to express the stone upwards, because of which the urine is released;
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with the instrument called a "syringe," of which this is the form:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and let it be of fine silver, lightly feathered, like the feather of a bird;
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and let the tube be a palm and a half long, and let it be slender at the end.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the manner of the evacuation of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie a bit of wool or cotton to the end, and put the end of the thread inside the syringe;
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and cut off the excess wool and put it up to the end of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, and have the patient sit on a seat, and moisten the bladder and penis with warm oil, olive oil, and warm water;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis upwards towards the belly;
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	then push the syringe forward to the bladder, and the patient will feel it reach the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order except because the conduit where it goes is twisted;
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then pull the thread with the wool little by little, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out completely, and let the urine flow;
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and repeat with the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	Of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When abrasions or blood come into the bladder, or putrefaction is gathered there, and you wish to instill waters and medicines, do so with the instrument which is called a “clepsydra,” and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and has three openings:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	Two on one side, and one on the other, as you see;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and the hollow through which the medicine flows should be such that it stops the penis well without addition, so that one may draw out the moisture, and insert it when necessary;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	And when you wish to pour your medicines into the bladder, place the head of the catheter in the moisture, and draw with the drawer which is inside;
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	you will draw the moisture with the catheter, and then forcefully push the drawer back in;
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	then the moisture will enter, and will reach the bladder immediately, so that the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and this is the form of the subtle clyster with which one clysterizes the bladder:
si est ci:	thus it is:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And it is of silver or of tin, and the head is higher;
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and below is a tube where the liquid falls;
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a sheep's bladder and put in it the liquid with which you wish to clysterize the bladder, then tie it between the two tubes firmly with a good double thread, and slightly heat that liquid over the fire;
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	then put the head of the clyster into the penis, then press your hand on the bladder with all the liquid gently, until the patient feels that the liquid has reached the bladder;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you do not have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make a circle from it, and pierce it roundly all around;
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	then put a strong thread in these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a bowl, and put inside what you wish of oil and liquid and water, and tie it to the instrument;
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the liquid reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have already spoken in the division of the types of stones, and their extraction along with medicines;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and I have spoken of the difference between the stone formed in the kidneys, and all the signs, and which stone one should operate on by cutting;
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the penis;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone which is formed in the bladder happens more often to children, and it is a sign that the urine leaps from the bladder similar to water in its subtlety;
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and sand appears, and the patient scratches his penis, and it hangs down many times, and then stiffens;
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and in many of these, the anus leaks;
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and the healing of children is easy until they are four years old, and it is very difficult in the elderly, and it is moderate in young adults, in those who are between youth and old age;
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with a clyster, to remove all the feces that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes hinders the extraction of the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the feet, and raise and move him downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes protrudes from its higher position;
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	then make him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands should be under his thighs, so that the bladder is completely inclined downwards;
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	then search for and touch it inside;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	if you feel the stone in the space, hasten now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not fall completely to the touch, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is a fully grown young man;
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and put it into his rectum, and search for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, guide it to the neck of the bladder;
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	then press down on it with your finger, and push it to the outside where you want to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and instruct him to lift the testicles with his right hand, and with his left hand remove the skin that is under the testicles in the area where the incision is made;
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	then insert the cutting spatula, of which this is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And cut between what is between the testicles and the rectum, not in the middle but to the left side of the perineum;
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and it should be directly over the stone, and your fingers should always be at the rectum, and the incision should be transverse so that it is wide on the outside, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	perhaps press with the finger that is in the rectum, so that it comes out without effort;
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and know that there are stones which have angles and edges:
si est griés a issir;	then it is difficult to remove;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and there are some which are smooth, similar to an acorn, and round, whose removal is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	Therefore, for one with angles and edges, make the incision larger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not come out, it is necessary that you extract it with forceps which are like a file at the head, to move the stone so that it does not escape;
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	or you place underneath it a thin instrument curved at the head;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot manage it thus, enlarge the hole a little, and if the blood flows, restrain it with vitriol;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there is more than one stone, put the largest one first at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then pull it out, and the small ones afterwards if there are several.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be sawn, and a larger incision made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	either he dies, or the urine constantly leaks because the wound cannot heal;
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but nevertheless try to pull it out, or break it with tongs, until you extract it in pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have completed your work, fill the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and place on top a cloth moistened in oil and wine, or in oil and rosewater and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess;
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	then support the patient on his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, irrigate the area very well with oil and water, then treat it with diafinicon ointment and basilicon ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if hot abscesses and corrosions appear in the wound, and blood clots in the bladder, and the urine is retained because of this, which is known in this way that it comes out with the urine without a jump:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	then put your finger in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains there, it will run to the bladder, and rot it;
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then clean the wound with water, vinegar, and salt, and help it in every way that you know, until it is healed;
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	and it is necessary that every time you treat it, you bind the two thighs together, and apply the medicines to the area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra, and lodged inside, and the urine cannot come out;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	then treat it as I said before, that you cut it many times, and one is excused from the incision by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this so.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron drill according to this form and let it be with three angles fixed in a firebrand:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot return to the bladder;
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	then insert the drill into the penis lightly, until it reaches the stone;
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and turn the drill in the stone with your hand little by little, until you can pierce the stone on the other side;
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	then the urine will come immediately, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then it is immediately broken, and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is cured;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	and if you cannot do this because of something that prevents it, then tie a thread under the stone and another above, then cut the penis towards the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	Of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	It rarely happens that a stone is generated in women, and if it happens sometimes, the cure is difficult, and is forbidden for three reasons:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second is that one cannot find a knowledgeable woman who will uncover herself to the physicians, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third reason is that perhaps one cannot find a woman well-skilled in this art nearby;
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	and the fourth reason is that the stone in a woman is deeper than the stone in a man, wherefore a deeper incision is necessary, and there is great danger. And if necessity demands this, then you must take a skilled female physician, and one scarcely finds them, and if you do not find one, at least seek a subtle chaste physician;
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and present to her a wise woman experienced in the lives of women, or a woman who knows some part of the art, and instruct her to do what you instruct her concerning the examination of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and look very carefully if the woman is a virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then she must insert her finger into the rectum and search for the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, she should compress it beneath her finger, and instruct the patient to place her finger in her vagina, and press her left hand strongly against the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	If she finds it, then she must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder downwards, until it reaches the groin;
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then cut towards the stone at the groin towards the middle of the vagina, where the muscle is prepared, and the stone is felt in that part;
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move her finger above or below the stone, and let the first incision be small;
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then put the instrument into the incision, if you feel the stone then enlarge the wound so that the stone can come out, and know that there are many types of stones:
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	that is to say, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and those which have roots.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	so know the similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the blood overcomes you, then put crushed vitriol in its place, and hold it for an hour until the bleeding is stopped;
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	then return to your work, until the stone is out, and have the instruments that I have told you about in the extraction of the stone in men to help you in your work;
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if the blood overcomes you, and it is from the artery which is cut, then put the powder on the place and restrain it with tents and bandages, and do not recommence that, and leave the stone and do not extract it, lest by chance the patient die;
puis cure la plaie.	then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is subsided, and the place is dried, then return to your work, until the stone is out.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Watery hernia is nothing else than an assembly of moisture or white humor, which is under the skin of the scrotum, which contains the testicle;
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and it is called "syfac," and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the testicle, so that one thinks that it is another testicle;
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and that is the skin of the scrotum between the white humor that we have mentioned;
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and this happens only rarely.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia is from weakness that comes to the testicles, and that matter is spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the testicles, and this moisture has many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or it is a color tending towards jaundice, or it is without redness, or black, or watery white, and this happens more;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to recognize this collection, for if it is in the white membrane that we have mentioned, the abscess is round, somewhat long like the shape of an egg, and the testicle does not appear, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the proper tunic, the abscess is round with a part of the testicle, and therefore it is thought to be another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white membrane, one feels it well;
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	therefore when you wish to know the color of the moisture, test it with a completely square probe, of which the form is shown above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to that then which comes after the probe, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be bled according to his ability and the repletion of his body;
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	then lay him on his back, on something a little high, and place many cloths underneath him;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left, and instruct the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs of the heart near the testicles;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the prepared spatula, and cut the skin of the scrotum along its length to near the handle, and let your incision be straight in separating the skin of the scrotum to the white fascia, and peel it carefully as much as you can;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	then pierce the fascia full of water with one large hole, and draw out all the water, and then apply your ointments, and stretch the fascia upwards;
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	and do not touch the testicles themselves, but only the fascia;
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	cut all or parts of it carefully on the side, because if you do not cut it skillfully, the water will return;
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if a testicle jumps out during your work, replace it in its place when you have completed the work on the fascia;
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then join the two lips of the scrotum with a suture, then treat it like other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the testicle corrupted by another illness, you must tie the vessels that are suspensory, to prevent the flow of blood;
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	then cut the testicle with all the suspensory ligament, and remove the testicle, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if water is gathered in two parts together, know that these are two branches;
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	then cut the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe the blood, and put in the wound wool moistened in rose oil;
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put on top more wool moistened in wine and oil, and place it over the two testicles, and put on top doubled cloths, and bind it all up with a bandage which is according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths, and fill them with carded wool according to this image and let them be joined by sewing at the opening of the breeches, and one of the ends should reach from the fundament to the back, and the other to the part of the groin;
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two ends over the two angles, and let the whole bandage be fastened in the loop of the breeches;
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and sometimes this area is treated with cautery instead of an iron incision, and it is that you take a thin, knife-like cauterizing instrument, and cut the skin of the testicles, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white layer that contains the water is uncovered;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that layer with the awl, and scrape it with this hot, thin cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And cut it in every way that you can, until you have scraped it all away;
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and take care that the fire does not touch the testicle;
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	and know that this procedure is safer;
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and more careful to avoid blood loss, and gentler than cutting procedures;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if anything goes against you, whether an abscess, or bleeding, or something else, then treat what opposes you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the patient is fearful, and does not want to undergo this procedure because of its horror, then administer perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are certain by the signs that we have mentioned that watery humor is present, then have the patient sit on a raised seat;
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	then pierce the abscess in the lower part with a spatula as wide as possible, and make the perforation along the length of the body;
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	and let the hole be wide, so that all the water may run out;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the place, and bind it, and let the remaining water drain, then treat it until the wound is healed;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	And if the white linen does not allow the water to escape from the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a feather or the instrument with which one draws water from the dropsical, the form of which is given above;
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and enlarge the wound a little, and know that the water returns and collects after six months or thereabouts, and when it is collected as before, and thus the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the section of this branch there is fear in many cases, wherefore it seems to me that it is better to leave it;
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the procedure and the characteristics of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I say then that many abscesses come in the body, and especially in the testicles;
et c’est par mout de cas.	and this is due to many causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	That is to say, by an excess of sour and sharp humor, which is spread to the testicles, or from a blow;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body;
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and it finds no pain, and it is a serious abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and perhaps some abscesses are serious, dangerous, and suppurating, and of a livid color, and sometimes come from an artery, or from a vein swelling.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from an artery, it is known by the disposition of a hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it is not necessary that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	That which is made from a vein swelling is known by its disposition to expression from the touch of the fingers, and one can well make the incision on this and other similar flesh;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut the heart of the testicles, then extend the egg upwards, and draw the white sheath strongly, and free the suspensory ligament from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the egg is already soldered with the neighboring flesh, then it is necessary that you draw out the egg, and cut it;
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is attached to the sheath, or in that which is within the vessels, then it is necessary that you free all that membrane, and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the origin of the flesh is in the posterior location, then it is necessary that you cut it all, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess enveloped in a covering similar to a bud, with softening of the testicles, and the patient moves with difficulty when he walks;
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and the treatment of this illness is almost as frightening as the one before, and yet we will tell you how to treat it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a raised seat, then place the suspensory of the testicles below your fingers, with all the vessels that are close to the penis, and let your master hold them, and extend them firmly;
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	then cut with a sharp, wide spatula across the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then scrape on each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries which are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then insert a needle with double thread, and tie it at the first point where the pus appeared, and tie it again at the other end;
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then cut them in the middle straight, according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted humors;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then treat the wound like the others where one inserts a tent, so that no vessel is cut which nourishes one of the testicles;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for by this no harm comes, and if pus comes to all the vessels, it is necessary to draw out the testicles with all the vessels;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the testicle does not lose its nourishment because of the incision of the vessels, and dries up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the rupture of the scrotum
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The occurrence of this hernia is by the section which happens in the scrotum, or the extension over the belly in the groin area, because of which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the testicles;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	and this rupture is either in the scrotum, or from the extension of it, and these two types come from many causes:
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	from a blow, or a jump, or a fall, or lifting a heavy weight, and by similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is from the extension of the scrotum, is that it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the swelling is even down to the bottom, because the scrotum presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is that when it is from the rupture of the scrotum, it causes sudden pain at the beginning, and the swelling is variously apparent, under the skin near, and this is because of the protrusion of the intestine and the body at the bottom of the scrotum.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the testicle descends with the intestine, and is held there, and causes the patient great pain to suffer, especially when it is pressed.
