Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments there is fear, wherefore one must be wary.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the work is that you instruct the patient to push the intestine back into place with his hand into the wound, if he can return it;
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then let it be supported at its neck between your hands, and raise the thighs;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then stretch the scrotum upwards, and cut all the skin of the testicles lengthwise;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then insert hooks into the edges of the wound according to what you need to open the wound, and let them be such that the egg may come out;
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then peel the fascia which is under the skin of the testicles, until the hard white fascia is uncovered on all sides;
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	then put your index finger into that which follows the testicle, into that which is between the white fascia which is under the skin of the egg, and between the second fascia, and separate that which is behind the egg, and between the second fascia;
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and then move your right hand into the scrotum, and stretch the white fascia upwards with your left hand, and lift the egg with all the fascia towards the groin;
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and instruct the assistant to extend the egg upwards, and loosen that which is behind the ligature;
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and search with your fingers if there is any intestine wrapped in the hard white fascia, and if you find anything, then put it back into the abdomen below;
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten threads, and put it into the back part of the fascia, which is behind the skin of the scrotum;
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	after the groin, then cut the ends of the threads that appear, until there are four threads;
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;	then assemble them one over the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the fascia, of which we have spoken, which is under the skin of the scrotum, with a strong ligature of two parts;
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then wrap the ends of the threads, and tie them firmly in two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter, lest an abscess should form there;
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and place the ligature again according to the first ligature, two fingerbreadths from it; and after these two ligatures, leave of the fascia which is under the skin of the scrotum the width of one finger;
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte;	and afterwards all the rest according to the roundness that the testicle bears;
puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	then cut in the part which is under the skin of the scrotum, until the blood runs, and the bowel, as we have said before;
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then apply wool soaked in oil, and place it in the wound, and apply the ligature that we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white fascia that we have mentioned is cauterized, after the incision, for fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui;	For this happens many times, and leave the ligature until it falls off by itself;
et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	and if it is slow to fall off, let it be sprinkled with warm water, and apply what we have said, until it falls off;
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then treat the wound with other treatments, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I never saw anyone who dared to perform the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is done like the branch which is next to the vein, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after cutting above or slightly below;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient;	then cut it in half, and treat the abscess with those who operate, until the vessels bleed;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the angles, as we have said, and the place opens;
et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	and none of the intestines descend to the testicles, and if some do descend, it is little, and returns every hour;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and yet if it remains too long in this state, the wound or fistula grows, until the intestine descends;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens because of the extension of the sheath which is at the angles, as we have said, for it is extended, then the place softens and swells and opens;
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit;	and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before;
et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois;	and that the patient lies often on his back between your hands, then cut the swollen place of the rupture, wide according to the quantity of three fingers;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the sheath which is under the skin that follows it, then take a root and put it on the apparent place of the sheath;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press it to the depth of the belly, then sew the two apparent places of the sheath over the head of the root, and sew one and the other;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then extract the head of the root, and do not cut the sheath nor extend the egg nor anything else, as I have let you know in the treatment of the hernia of the intestines;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	then cure it by the cure of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, then cleanse and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The sheath is constricted, and there is no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is gentler in this place, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the scrotum skin
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Many times the scrotum skin is softened in some men, because the flesh within is softened, and it is ugly to see;
et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil;	and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and cuts the softened skin from the natural skin;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement;	then bring the two lips together with a suture, and if you wish, first cut away the excess of the softened skin with three or four sutures firmly;
puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	then cut between the sutures, and cure it like other wounds, until it is healed, and the thread comes out.
dou chastrement	Of castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	Know that castration is forbidden in our law, and therefore I would prefer not to speak of it in this book;
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and it is only necessary for two reasons:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	one is that the surgeon knows how to respond when asked, and knows the treatment;
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other, because we often need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	I say then that castration is done in two ways:
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	either by pulling, or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In that which we do by pulling, we make the animal sit in warm water until the testicles are softened and hanging;
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	then take them in your hand until they are retracted and you feel them no more.
Du chastrement de taille:	Of castration by cutting:
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	you must hold the animal, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory, and cut on each testicle with one cut, when you have well skinned them;
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	and leave some pouch of the tunica vaginalis and the thin membrane which is over the vessels;
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	and this method of castration is better than that which is done by pulling, because in pulling, by chance, some part of the testicles remains, wherefore the animal desires lust;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Of the hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Hermaphroditism is according to two manners in men:
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	one is that between the two testicles appears something like the figure of a woman's nature, where there is hair, and sometimes the urine flows there.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and she has above the vulva something like a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the cure of the man and the woman is that you cut away all the added flesh, and cure it like other wounds;
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	in the second manner, of men whose urine escapes through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tenesmus
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	Tenesmus is a growth added to the natural part, so that it is too ugly to see;
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	It is necessary that you hold the superfluity of the tenesmus in your hand or with tongs, and cut it lightly;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do not go too deep, lest a flow of blood come from it, then cure it with another cure until it is healed;
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	and another growth that arises at the mouth of the womb, and fills it, and perhaps bursts forth, and is in the likeness of a cow, and for this reason the ancients called it "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then you must cut it, as we have said of the tenesmus, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	Erratic is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small;
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	and is natural by birth, or accidental by a disease that has come to it;
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	or it is by added flesh, or by a thin or thick septum, and is made deeply in the womb, or on the sides, or underneath, or wherever it may be;
et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir;	and prevents conception, and childbirth, and perhaps the having of menses;
et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	and the knowledge of this is by the examination of the vagina.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the stoppage is near, I search with my fingers or with a probe.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	If it is of a thin septum, and it is near the two lips, then hasten, and break it thus:
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	place your two index fingers together, and the woman should be on her back, her legs spread;
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	then stretch the two lips widely, until the thin septum is broken, and the stoppage is opened;
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and place it on the spot, and let the woman lie with a man each day, so that it may not heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the septum is hard and thick, then you must cut it with a spatula similar to a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If the stoppage is of raw flesh, then suspend it with a hook and cut it;
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	and have styptic medicines, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, together with egg white;
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	then apply a wide lead splint, so that the wound cannot heal;
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	and so it should be for a long time, and apply a tent of dry linen;
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let it be cured with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the wound comes new flesh, then it is necessary to cut it according to this manner, unless it is festering abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For a festering abscess which is in the wound, one should not touch with fire.
des emorroides	of the hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins from which blood often flows, and when the hemorrhoids are old they become swollen.
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	and we have already said in the division the similar things of these, and the signs, and I will say here those which receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and swellings, when they are deep in the wound and do not appear to the touch, are not cured by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those which are at the opening of the wound, that one can feel, are those which one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	It is necessary then that you place the woman in a cold house, then grasp the swelling with tongs, and cut it at its roots, then sprinkle on medicines that staunch blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things;
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	then place her feet against the wall for an hour, then place her in cold water;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	and if a flow of blood occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster of it and put it on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If not, apply cupping glasses to the back and breasts without cutting;
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	then take wool, and moisten it in plantain juice or agrimony juice with old wine, and apply it to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when the abscess is healed, treat the place with ointment until it is healed;
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to a rough head, so it must be cut as I have said of the thelul;
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of the abscesses of the sea
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses arise in the sea, such as cancer and stony abscess and herpes and esthiomenes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	It is necessary then that I discuss in this treatise the hot abscess which comes in the sea, which is not of the abscesses which collect pus;
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	and if you wish to know the work of iron, see if the abscess is acute at the beginning of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Then do not hasten to pierce it, but let it mature until the pain is lessened;
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	and then have the patient sit on a seat, and have two small seats where he leans, and rests on his back and brings his feet together at the outer parts of the legs;
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	and let his thighs be spread, and put his arms under his knees, and bind them well with a good band;
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	then suck him towards the right side, and administer the instrument with which one opens the mouth of the abscess, of which the form follows;
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	and it is necessary that when you see this instrument administered, that you first insert a probe to know the depth of the abscess, so that that which enters the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not injure the patient;
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the abscess with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm it;
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	and it is necessary that he put the cone of the instrument on top, and that he hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscess is opened, and one feels it with a soft hand, then it is necessary to cut it at the head, at the spatula-like point;
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	and when the boil is emptied, it is necessary that you place in the wound tents soaked in rose oil, or in dry green oil;
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	and place the tent deep within the abscess, and place on the outside of the abscess and on the wound clean wool soaked in water in which mallows have been cooked;
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it after two days with an ointment suitable for this, until it is healed;
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	and sometimes one cleans the abscess and the wound with a clyster of water and honey, and then of water in which lily roots and long birthwort have been cooked;
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is hidden in the abscess, then you must refrain from cautery with iron, but treat it as we have said in the chapter.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	It is first necessary for the midwife to know the form of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman straining downwards, and desiring to push.
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	then the child hastens to come out;
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	then know that that childbirth is according to the natural form, and the exit is head first, and the afterbirth with it;
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her belly, so that the child comes out quickly;
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	for when it descends head first, the afterbirth comes out with it, and the womb is cleansed of its superfluities by good cleansing;
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	and that which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	For sometimes it comes feet first, and the body or head and hands are forced out, or it comes on its belly, or sideways, and is perhaps twisted around its neck, and in other bad positions;
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	so it is necessary for the midwife that she be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the positions how one should help her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If the child comes head first by natural issue, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, then make her sit on a saddle, where the women hold her;
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	and anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek which has been cooked, and then let the midwife put between her fingers the small spatula of which here is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	and split the secundine, and cut with her nail until the moisture which is inside runs out;
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	and grasp the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to give the woman a clyster of fenugreek mucilage with sesame oil;
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	then make her sneeze and cough with a potion, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour:
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	then the child will come out immediately.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if the two hands come out, then it is necessary that you gently replace them little by little;
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	and if they cannot be put back in, then put the woman on a chair, and raise her feet upwards;
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	then bring the chair down to the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not fall when it is brought down;
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and if the hands cannot be put back in, and the child dies, then cut the hands with the knife that is placed here in front, and extract the child, and replace them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the delivery of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes on its feet, then it is necessary to push it upwards;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it little by little, until it is even;
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take one of the feet and extend it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	When it comes down to the thighs, then instruct to grasp it, and make it sneeze with a potion;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it jumps further, if God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not go further as we have said, then turn it little by little, until it is according to the natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it comes out easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier;	And if it does not come out as we have said, then take mallow mucilage, and linseed oil, and melted gum, and grind everything in a mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	and put it on the woman's vulva and melt this ointment, then make her sit in warm water up to the ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is softened below, make her a pessary of myrrh, and put it below, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make her sit on a seat, then make her sneeze and squeeze her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for the child will jump out immediately.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child's exit onto her knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this way, the midwife should put her hands in little by little;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit;	then let it be supported by its neck, and its feet hanging down, and let it lie on a bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and bend its hands little by little, and then take its hands over its belly, and remove the cushions from below, until it is positioned downwards;
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the child does not come out, take its feet and move them strongly, then move its belly upwards, then put your hands in;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc;	and draw the child out little by little;
et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and instruct the woman to strain until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the delivery of the child that comes from the womb, a hand appearing first
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to contrive to bring back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if one cannot bring it back, then make the woman stand up and walk;
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, then make her lie on the bed, and raise her legs strongly;
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then administer the mucilage that I have described;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a seat, then work at bringing back the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and draw the child according to its natural position, and make her sneeze, and instruct her to strain until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the child's exit over its neck, and its hands spread out, and its face turned towards its mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	it is necessary that the midwife hold its hand, then turn it little by little, and draw it gently;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, then apply to the place a poultice of mallow and oil, as we have said, then instruct her to move little by little;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne;	and when you have done this, then make her sit on a seat, and instruct her to strain;
et la fai esternuer.	and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner with all the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes out in this manner with all the afterbirth, then cut the afterbirth with your nail, until the moisture is emptied;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child hangs by its face and neck, then cut it from the buttocks, so that it is not retained, and the child dies;
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the child inside, until you have placed it as is fitting, and instruct the woman that she should take herself sometimes:
adonques si istra legierement.	then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	Of the delivery of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	Know that twins are often born, and sometimes three or four are born;
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	and that is not a strange thing, and it happens little.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two is a strange thing, and they do not live, except very few;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they are multiplied, and are separated by the syfac which divides them, which is attached to the womb;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they come out as naturally as a single one, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they come out with difficulty, treat them as we have said, and let the hand be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what she does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do so as it is worth moving to salvation.
de plusors enfans	of several children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	Sometimes they are formed in the womb, one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more up to fifteen, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise glorious, and the hand must know all this, for by chance similar things happen;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	then do according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat a woman with a dead child in her womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	it is necessary that the woman be placed on her back, and her head inclined down, and her legs raised;
et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the assistant hold her from two sides, or she be tied to the bed so that she is not pulled during the descent of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils with mallow and fenugreek mucilage and linseed, then oil her hands with these oils and mucilages;
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	then put them into the womb lightly, then find a place where she puts the ointments that are suitable for this, and take care if the child is positioned to descend head first;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	then insert the ointments into its eyes or into its neck or into its mouth or onto its palate or under the chin or into the clavicle or near the ribs, and if the descent is feet first, then insert them into the heel and the middle ribs;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he hold the ointment with his right hand, and place the curvature between the fingers of his left hand, and put it in with his whole hand lightly, and insert the ointment into one of these places that we have mentioned, until it reaches the empty space;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the ointment:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then insert another ointment against it, or a third if you need it, so that the extractions are equal;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then spread it equally by moving from one side to the other, so that the pus comes out, and let the ointments be toothed to hold the pus, as the shape is here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if some remains, let him moisten some of his fingers with oil, and put them into that part, and draw out the other part;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if any remains, put this ointment on a higher place, and do this until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	And if one hand comes before the other, and he cannot bring it back because of the tightness, then you must wrap it in a cloth until it all comes out;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	then cut it at the joint of the sole or at the heel, and thus you must do in the other hand, and in the two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	And if the child's head is large and it is narrow at the exit, or it has an accumulation of watery fluid in the head, then you must put the pointed spatula between your fingers, and split the head and draw out the water;
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you round it with the instrument that is called "almidach", the form of which comes with the instruments in the chapter which is after this one;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and do the same if the child has a naturally large head;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and then pull out the bones with tongs, and if the head jumps out and is extracted with the forceps, let it be split, until the moisture that is in the worst part issues forth;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot come out, cut it into pieces as best you can;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce it until the moisture runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the extraction is easy, and the straightening at the mouth of the womb is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is narrow in the belly or chest, then you must extract it with a cloth wrapped around the hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and open the belly or chest, until the moisture that is there runs out;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	and if the other limbs are removed, and the head remains, then the midwife puts her hand deep into the womb, and draws it out to the mouth of the womb;
puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer;	then puts in one or two fingers, and pulls it strongly;
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	and if the mouth of the womb is constricted by a hot abscess that has formed there, then you must not work there, but must administer moist and oily things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and apply plasters, and sit in softening and moistening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is on its side, and you can put it straight, then administer what we have said for a living child;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if one does not have the power, then pull it out forcefully piece by piece, and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, then administer what we have said for hot abscesses that occur in the womb;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if a flow of blood comes, then it should be put in astringent water, and administer other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb a child had been dead, then another was conceived upon that one, and the other was also dead.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came to her in the groin, and it swelled until it opened, and began to greatly suppurate.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the treatment, and I thought about it for a long time, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a plaster of strong attraction, and a bone came out, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised, because the womb has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	So I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point;	I cleaned the wound, and extracted more bones, until the woman was in better condition;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman lived a long time like that, and a little pus always came out of the place;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have recorded this chapter only because, when the master finds something strange, that he should know how to provide help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	of returning the marrow to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	After this comes the form of the press, with which one binds the books;
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and with two turnings at the two ends of the two bands.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns should be more slender than the restrictor, and should be made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the opening of the wood should be one inch wide, and the edge of the boards one inch, and one and a half palms long;
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and between the two bands should be two additions of this same wood, which should be fastened to one and the other, half a palm long or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	and these two additions are inserted into the opening of the trepan to open when the two horns are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, similar but more slender and lighter, should be made of ebony or boxwood, in the likeness of tongs;
et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	and have at the two ends two additions, as you see, one palm long, and two inches wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	and when you wish to open the trepan with the whole instrument, have the woman sit on a bed, her feet hanging down and her legs open, then put the two attached additions into the trepan, and hold the head of the instrument underneath between her thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand with the whole instrument, just as you did with the tongs equally, according to the amount that you wish to open the mouth of the trepan, until the opening does what it should.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	These instruments are all surpassed, and their forms are multiplied;
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	and when the surgeon has prepared them, the work is all the quicker, and higher for men because of their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument that you have not prepared, for their necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the afterbirth is retained in childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze with a potion, and press your hands to her mouth and nose;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if it comes out because of this, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, take a pot, and make a hole in the lid, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia lignea, and centaury;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	all these herbs, or some of them, should be boiled in water in the pot over the fire;
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	then put one end of a tube in the hole of the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the womb, and hold it there until the vapors enter the womb;
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secundines come out quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	And if it remains after this treatment, and does not come out, instruct the midwife to wet her left hand in sesame oil or mallow poultice, and then put it into the vagina, and search for the secundines;
et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and when she has found it, let her take it and gently extend it straight, so that the womb does not fall during extraction;
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie;	but it should be moved lightly to the right and to the left, and then pulled;
si venra et se desaerdra.	then it will come and detach itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the womb is too narrow, we have mentioned the treatment of sneezing and herbal fumigation;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it does not come out from all that we have said, be careful not to be rash in pulling;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the womb, you tie it to the thigh of the woman, then you administer a clyster of tetrafarmacon ointment;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	then it will rot and soften, and come out.
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	But nevertheless, when it rots, a bad odor comes to the stomach and the head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	Then suitable fumigations are necessary for this:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Some of the ancients have tested a fumigation of cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for the retention of the flowers and the afterbirth is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is of glass similar to a funnel, and one puts the narrow end into the vagina, and the wide end over the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigation be on the coals, and burn it until it is consumed, and begin again with another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the fundament pierced, but it is stopped up by a thin membrane:
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	then it is necessary for the midwife that she pierce that membrane with her finger, and not pierce it with a sharp instrument, and she must be careful that she does not injure it;
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply wool soaked in wine and oil, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will close up again, put a lead tube in the opening and leave it there for several days, and it should be removed when the child wants to use the toilet.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And sometimes this obstruction comes suddenly from a wound or an abscess;
si covient coper celui soudement:	then it is necessary to cut that obstruction.
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	then it should be treated, as we have said with the lead tube.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistulas which come from under the fundament are knotting, and swelling which come beside the fundament outwardly, or in the space of the two parts, then there is one fistula or several;
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	and when that knotting is old, it works, and then discharges white moisture or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas are perforating;
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and are known by this, that there comes out with the excretion or flatulence when the patient excretes, and by chance a worm jumps out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And there are fistulas which pierce as far as the bladder, and as far as the middle of the penis;
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and reach as far as the joint of the thigh, and as far as the buttock.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows the perforating fistula at the fundament, and not the non-perforating:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you put your index finger in the fundament, and put a fine needle of bronze or iron in the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is tortuosity, then put in a thin lead probe, or a horsehair, until you feel the probe or the hair at your finger;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge of excretion or flatulence or worm from the opening, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	know that it does not perforate;
si te haste dou curer.	then hasten to the cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is perforating to the bladder or to the urinary duct, then the urine leaks out, and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced to the hip joint, then the tent is coming to the place;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no tortuosity and the location of the pain around, it is that it always swells, and neither medicine nor healing by ointment helps;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these perforating fistulas there is no cure but labor, and the vanity of foolish physicians who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In that which is not perforating and is not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies on his back between your hands;
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and he lifts his legs up to his thighs, and has his thighs inclined towards his belly;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then place a tent of bronze, or of lead if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tent comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you must put your index finger there, if you then feel that the tent has pierced it;
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and it is uncovered where you feel between your finger the pus or the flesh, then know that it is perforating;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	then do not work on it if it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	It is said however that one can heal some, but this happens rarely;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help that is done, is that one heats the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it is said before;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	and puts it very hot into the fistula, until it reaches near the bottom;
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and do this two or three times, until you know that the rotten flesh is burned, which is similar to a bird's feather;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then treat it with tents soaked in butter, until that rotten flesh comes out, then treat it with an ointment that generates flesh and heals.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If this, it cannot be healed otherwise;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the tent enters, and does not pierce to the finger which is in the bottom, and there is between your finger and the tent a thick covering of flesh or of syfac, and you see the fistula at that which follows the covering of the heart;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push the tent forward, and then cauterize afterwards, until it reaches the head of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	and the tent will be delivered, and will fall;
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	then cleanse those rotten fleshes that resemble a bird's feather, and let nothing remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood overcomes you, and flows between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or with a sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For fire cautery combines two good things:
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	that is to say, the burning of these added fleshes, and the stanching of blood and the drying of moisture;
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then cure it with tents moistened in butter or in crushed herbs, until the place throws off pus, and the burnt flesh emerges in the pus;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then treat the wound with ointments that heal hard flesh, and these are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula goes down to the bottom of the fundament, and is far from the body, put your finger into the fundament, and investigate that.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel the tent, and between two is the membrane or the fascia or flesh, where it is about to pierce, there should be no fear but confidence and hope, through the administration of one of three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can, put tents there and treat it as before;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too deep, lest you cut the ligament that holds the fundament, and there is an evacuation against the will;
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then treat it, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it after it is cut near the fundament, either with a tent or another pointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then cleanse that rotten flesh which is in the wound, as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	then strive to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the part outside the fundament:
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	this will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And sometimes fistulas are like this:
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and it is when you place the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the fundament near the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the head in this way:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And put one twisted thread into two, and put the tent with the thread into the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is penetrating into the margin of the fundament inside, then pull the thread from that hole, so that you put your finger into the fundament;
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	and pull the end of the thread, and bring the two ends together, and pull one to the other, and leave it one or two days;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it sometimes, until the thread cuts the flesh that is between them, and they come together;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then treat the wound until it is healed and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in every way that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not necessary to cut too deeply for the ligation, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spatumile espinous with which one opens the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other side not, so that one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of the hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	Hemorrhoids are according to two manners:
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	or they are inside the fundament, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they constantly bleed, and there is one or more, and they are outside the fundament and at the end of the fundament;
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those which are outside have little moisture, and constantly leak a little citrine water or a little blood, and have the color of the flesh;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the cure of those who have them inside the fundament, is that you instruct the patient to strain to go to the privy, until the fundament comes out, and the threads appear;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	then hurry, and grasp it with tongs, or hold it with your fingernail, then cut it at its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the hooks cannot hold them because of their moisture, then grasp them with a rag, or with cotton, or a piece of chamois leather;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and pull them out with your fingers, then cut them, and sprinkle on some hot powders that are in place of a cautery;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as is said in the chapter on cautery, then treat them with other treatments until they are healed;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the matter cannot come out, then give the patient a clyster of a biting and harsh clyster to wash what is in the fundament, so that it may come out clearly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the patient is seized, and if the threads are strong from the fundament, then the cure is easy;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you take them with your fingernail or with tongs, and cut them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healed, and that one fears the incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	Then you must administer the suture according to this manner:
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	take a twisted thread, and put it in a needle, and then pull the thread above and make the needle pierce on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and so it should be wide;
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and pull the thread strongly, then knot the thread, and remove the needle, and do so for all the others, and leave one to drain the excess blood;
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the wound a cloth moistened in rose oil or cerate, and put it on the wound, and instruct the patient to rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it until they fall off, and when they have fallen off, treat them with ointment and other treatment, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the dryness of the feces or wound
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is dryness of feces in the intestine, and by natural constriction, and when the illness is old and medicine is of no use.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	Then you must scrape with the point of a spatula or your fingernail the crust above, which does not allow it to moisten;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat it until it is healed as is necessary;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot heal, then begin scraping again more forcefully than before, until it bleeds much and is scraped;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of the trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Formication is a small, crawling sensation around the body, and goes very deep;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes it feels cold, and it is felt as if dead from trembling, and it comes over the whole body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a quill from a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and put that quill on the trembling, until the circle encompasses the trembling entirely;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand with the quill until you cut all around the trembling, and put it deep in, and pull out the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do this with a quill of bronze or iron according to this form, and let it be thin below and broad above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	not pierced, so as to hold and press firmly with the finger.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you wish, cauterize the trembling, as is described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	Of the form of the clyster.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	Sometimes a clyster is made of silver, or of tin, or of molten or hammered bronze;
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and sometimes these instruments are made small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those therefore which are administered in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large clyster is wider above, where the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	and there is an opening where the belly is bound, as you see, and the end is pierced inside;
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	and has on one side two holes, and on the other one;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and let the belly, where one puts the medicines, be of an animal bladder or of parchment, and let it be pierced all around with small holes, and let there be one finger's breadth of space between each hole, then put into these holes a strong thread of raw thread twisted in an X or around, and assemble the belly as if it were a goatskin;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then clysterize;
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or egg white, or something similar, then insert it gently;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	then the attendant squeezes it with both hands together, until it is completely empty, then withdraw the clyster, and let the patient raise his legs against the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, let him hold it as long as he can;
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps a whole night, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clysterize him for a disease of bowel discharge, and the medicine quickly comes out, repeat it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are in the rectum, or an abscess, let the clyster be as fine as for a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the fine clyster on which the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have, I said in the division, the treatment of wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	or we will tell you the cures by hand and by medicine, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and what they are made of.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by the throwing of a stone, and the blow of a sword and of a knife, or of a lance or of a stick or of an arrow, or of similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the foot, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members;
